423 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


I. L. F. Y. Co. v. Temporary State Housing Rent Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


11 N.Y.2d 259; 183 N.E.2d 220; 228 N.Y.S.2d 814; 1962 N.Y. LEXIS 1169


March 26, 1962, Argued  
May 10, 1962, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgments and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, owners of rent controlled New York City residential properties, sought review of judgments of the Supreme Court at Special Term of New York County (New York), which granted motions by respondents, the Temporary State House Rent Commission and others, to dismiss the owners' complaints pursuant to N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 106(4) and of an order of the Supreme Court at Special Kings County (New York), which dismissed a proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The owners sought a declaration of unconstitutionality of an amendment, 1962 N.Y. Laws ch. 21, § 6, to the State Emergency Housing Rent Control Law, 1946 N.Y. Laws ch. 274, that prohibited any increase in rents, unless a tenant consented, for a period of two and one-half months from the effective date of the amendment. At the end of that period, New York City was to take over rent control administration within its boundaries. The trial courts held that 1962 N.Y. Laws ch. 21, § 6 was not violative of any constitutional rights of the owners, and the owners took direct appeals to the court. In affirming the decisions, the court held that the freeze in the rent increases for the relatively short period pending transfer of control to the city was reasonably incidental to such a change over and was constitutional. Further, the owners had no "vested" rights to increase orders or to continuation of the rules or formulae on which their applications had been based. The legislature concluded that one necessary or desirable condition of the concededly valid State-to-city rent regulatory power transfer was that there be a breathing spell during which no increase orders should be entered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments and order.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- constitutional law -- provision in 1962 amendment (L. 1962, ch. 21, § 6) to State Emergency Housing Rent Control Law, forbidding increase in regulated residential rents for period from effective date of amendment (Feb. 17, 1962) to May 1, 1962, reasonably incidental to transfer of rent control to city and not unconstitutional.

The 1962 amendments (L. 1962, ch. 21) to the State Emergency Housing Rent Control Law (L. 1946, ch. 274, as amd.) transfer rent control in the City of New York from the State to that city and require it to establish its own rent agency to carry on such control after May 1, 1962. Section 6 of the 1962 act forbids any increase (in the absence of consent) in regulated residential rents for the period from February 17, 1962, the effective date of the amendments, to May 1, 1962. The short delay ordered by the Legislature is reasonably incidental to the transfer of control to the city and the statute providing for such delay is not unconstitutional.

 

424 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Cannata v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


11 N.Y.2d 210; 182 N.E.2d 395; 227 N.Y.S.2d 903; 1962 N.Y. LEXIS 1201


February 26, 1962, Argued  
April 26, 1962, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant home owners sought review of a judgment the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which modified and affirmed the supreme court's judgment dismissing the home owners' complaint. The appellate division struck out the decretal paragraph dismissing the complaint in the home owners' action for judgment declaring N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 72-n unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Sixty-eight home owners brought an action for a declaratory judgment that § 72-n was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to the proposed redevelopment of the area in which the home owners lived. At least 75 percent of the area involved was vacant. Respondent city sought dismissal of the complaint and for summary judgment, and the supreme court held that the home owners were not entitled to relief. On appeal, the appellate division modified the judgment by directing judgment for the city rather than merely dismissal of the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the complaint did not allege any failure to carry out any of the statutory procedures, but rather the real basis of the complaint was that there was in the area no "tangible physical blight" as to constitute the area of slum. The court found, as did the courts below, that an area did not have to be a "slum" to make its redevelopment a public use, nor was public use negated by a plan to turn a predominantly vacant, poorly developed and organized area into a site for new industrial buildings. The court found nothing unconstitutional on the face of § 72-n or in its proposed application here.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate division's judgment, which modified the supreme court's judgment by directing judgment for the city, in the home owners' action to have a statute relating to area redevelopment unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- condemnation and redevelopment -- statute (formerly General Municipal Law, § 72-n), which authorities cities to condemn, for reclamation and redevelopment, predominantly vacant areas in condition which tends to develop slums and blighted areas, is not unconstitutional.

1. A statute (formerly General Municipal Law, § 72-n) which authorizes cities to condemn, for the purpose of reclamation or redevelopment, predominantly vacant areas which are economically dead so that their existence and condition impairs the sound growth of the community and tends to develop slums and blighted areas is not unconstitutional.

2. An area does not have to be a "slum" to make its redevelopment a public use. The condemnation by the city of an area such as that here involved under a plan to turn a predominantly vacant, poorly developed and organized area into a site for new industrial buildings is a public use.

 

425 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Boyd v. Collins


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


11 N.Y.2d 228; 182 N.E.2d 610; 228 N.Y.S.2d 228; 1962 N.Y. LEXIS 1203


March 28, 1962, Argued  
April 26, 1962, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent school board sought review of a judgment from the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which reversed an order of the supreme court that estopped the teacher from demanding restoration of her tenure rights and directed the school board to restore the teacher's position on the payroll with full tenure rights and with back pay.


OVERVIEW: The parents of students in the teacher's class presented informal complaints against the teacher, who had tenure. The president of the school district informed the teacher of the complaints and told her that she was not to teach any more. Another teacher was installed in the teacher's classroom. The school board then authorized an agreement in which it agreed to pay the teacher for the remainder of the year and to provide a good letter of recommendation. The principal wrote a letter that provided the dates and grades taught by the teacher but it did not provide a recommendation. The teacher filed a petition for reinstatement with back pay, which was denied by the supreme court. The appellate division reversed the supreme court's decision upon finding that the agreement was invalid because it was contrary to the tenure statute, N.Y. Educ. Law § 3013, and because it violated the constitutional ban against gifts of public moneys. N.Y. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The school board claimed on appeal that the agreement was valid. The court rejected the school board's claim. The court ruled that the agreement was invalid and that the school board failed to comply with the agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate division's order that the teacher be reinstated to her teaching position with restoration of tenure rights and with back pay.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- teachers -- tenure -- agreement whereby local school board attempted to discharge tenured teacher without charges or hearing by paying her year's salary for not teaching is in violation both of tenure law (Education Law, § 3013) and of constitutional prohibition against gifts of public moneys (N. Y. Const., art. VIII, § 1) -- board violated agreement -- teacher not estopped and not required to return salary.

1. In October, 1957, at a time when petitioner had tenure and was eligible for retirement and the local school board had renewed her contract for the school year 1956-1957, petitioner was told that the school board would pay her salary until the end of the term if she would resign and that she was relieved from duty. When she went to her classroom she found another teacher there. The president of the school board told petitioner that she was entitled to a hearing and she stated that she wished to have one. At a meeting thereafter conducted, at which petitioner was not present but at which a lawyer who had not been retained as her attorney spoke in her behalf, the school board authorized an arrangement for the payment to petitioner of her salary to the end of the year and stated that the board would give her "a good letter of recommendation". Petitioner never resigned and charges have never been filed against her or tried. It is a violation of tenure rights (Education Law, § 3013) to remove, without charges and hearing, a teacher who has tenure. To hold that, for a consideration, petitioner waived her right to a hearing would be contrary to the public policy of this State expressed in the tenure statutes.

2. Moreover, an agreement under which public money would be paid without services rendered on condition that charges be withheld and the teacher resign is an unconstitutional gift of public money (N. Y. Const., art. VIII, § 1).

3. The agreement was also invalid because the board never, in fact, complied with it. It did not give petitioner a letter of recommendation but merely an official statement as to the duration of her teaching career and the fact that she had the required qualifications.

4. Petitioner is not estopped from questioning the validity of the contract because she accepted its benefits. She got no benefits. Furthermore, public policy renders it doubtful whether estoppel can be invoked.

5. It is not necessary for petitioner to return the salary paid to her before she obtains relief. After she was told by the principal to stop teaching, she was under no obligation to present herself every morning for work since she had a valid permanent contract of employment.

 

426 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Siegal v. Dros


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


11 N.Y.2d 167; 182 N.E.2d 106; 227 N.Y.S.2d 431; 1962 N.Y. LEXIS 1253


February 27, 1962, Submitted  
April 5, 1962, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order of Appellate Division reversed and that of Special Term reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) reversed an order that sustained a writ of habeas corpus and that discharged defendant from prison. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the appellate division erred in reversing the lower court's order that granted the writ of habeas corpus. The court agreed, reversed the order of the appellate division, and reinstated the order of the special term that granted defendant a writ of habeas corpus and released him from prison. The court found that the information charging defendant with various housing code violations, and which also served as the basis for a warrant of arrest, was unsworn. The court found that where a defendant was convicted of a misdemeanor, rather than an offense of less than the grade of misdemeanor, an unsworn information was jurisdictionally defective and could not support a conviction. Accordingly, the court held that the proceedings were jurisdictionally defective and that the special term properly sustained the writ.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate division and reinstated the order of the special term that sustained the writ of habeas corpus, and discharged defendant from prison.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unsworn information -- unsworn information insufficient whether crime charged is misdemeanor or "offense" -- court without jurisdiction to try defendant on charges of violations of Multiple Dwelling Law ( §§ 78, 80) and Multiple Dwelling Code of City of New York (§§ D26-3.1, D26-3.2) on unsworn information.

1. The New York City Magistrates' Court was without jurisdiction to try appellant on the basis of an unsworn information charging him with violations of sections 78 and 80 of the Multiple Dwelling Law and sections D26-3.1 and D26-3.2 of the Multiple Dwelling Code of the City of New York.

2. Where a defendant is charged with a misdemeanor, as distinguished from an offense of less than the grade of misdemeanor, an unsworn information is jurisdictionally defective.

3. One offense of which appellant was convicted -- violation of section 80 of the Multiple Dwelling Law -- must be treated procedurally as a misdemeanor ( Multiple Dwelling Law, § 304, subd. 1-a). The legislative history of that statute makes it clear that the Legislature, in downgrading the violation of certain sections of the Multiple Dwelling Law from misdemeanors to offenses, intended to preserve to defendant all his prior procedural rights. Since the language of the statute is clear and unambiguous, and an unsworn information does not confer jurisdiction upon a court to try a misdemeanor, it follows that the court had no jurisdiction to try appellant on the basis of the unverified information.

4. Where, as here, the punishment for an "offense" could be a year's imprisonment in a State prison and a substantial fine, an "offense" cannot be said to be of such minor consequence that an unsworn information is sufficient.

 

427 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Schroeder v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 522; 180 N.E.2d 568; 225 N.Y.S.2d 210; 1962 N.Y. LEXIS 1411


December 6, 1961, Argued  
January 25, 1962, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff riparian owner challenged the decision of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed the order of the lower court granting the motion of defendant, the City of New York (city), for judgment on the pleadings, dismissed the complaint seeking to enjoin the city from diverting an upstream river, and denied the riparian owner's cross motion for judgment on the pleadings.


OVERVIEW: Seven years after the city commenced diversion of an upstream river pursuant to the Water Supply Act (Act), the riparian owner brought an action against the city to prevent it from diverting the river. The city filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings on the ground that the action was time-barred by her failure to file a claim within three years as required by New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § K41-18.0. The lower court granted the motion, dismissed the complaint, and denied the riparian owner's cross motion, and the appellate court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the notice requirements of New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § K41-8.0 satisfied due process because it called for frequent publication in public newspapers and in two newspapers published in each county where the affected real estate was located. The Act also provided for the posting of handbills for a period of time in conspicuous places near the aqueduct or the affected real estate. The court found that the city complied with the requirements of the Act. The court also found that the effect of the diversion was apparent to the riparian owner long before the three-year limitation expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city in an action brought by the riparian owner seeking to prevent the city from diverting a river upstream from her property.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- notice of diversion of river -- notice provisions of Water Supply Act (Administrative Code of City of New York, ch. 41, tit. K) do not contravene requirements of due process -- complaint properly dismissed where claim not filed within time limited (Administrative Code of City of New York, § K41-18.0).

1. The notice provisions of the Water Supply Act (Administrative Code of City of New York, ch. 41, tit. K) do not contravene the requirements of due process. Not only does the statute call for publication once a week for six weeks in two newspapers published in New York City and in two papers published in each county in which the real estate affected is located, but it also provides for the posting of handbills, for a period of six weeks, "in at least twenty conspicuous places on the line of the aqueduct or in the vicinity of the real estate so to be taken or affected" (§ K41-8.0).

2. Where the City of New York in June, 1952 became invested with the right to divert a portion of the Neversink River in Orange County, and the work on the actual diversion started in June of 1953, the complaint in an action commenced seven years thereafter to enjoin the city from diverting the river upstream from plaintiff's property was properly dismissed on the ground that the action was barred by plaintiff's failure to file a claim within the time limited, as required by the Water Supply Act (Administrative Code of City of New York, § K41-18.0). Moreover, the challenged diversion of the river was apparent long before the expiration of such period.

 

428 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Thacher v. United Constr. Workers, etc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 439; 180 N.E.2d 245; 224 N.Y.S.2d 657; 1962 N.Y. LEXIS 1468; 49 L.R.R.M. 2530; 44 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P17,451


December 7, 1961, Argued  
January 11, 1962, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed. Motion for stay denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trust fund sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) which affirmed an order of the trial court granting a petition by respondent Superintendent of Insurance of the State of New York for an order, pursuant to N.Y. Insurance Law § XVI, directing said superintendent to take possession of the property and liquidate and dissolve the affairs of the trust fund.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent of insurance brought a petition seeking an order allowing him to take possession of the property and liquidate the affairs of and dissolve a trust fund created for the employees of a defunct business pursuant to a collective bargaining agreement. The trustees of the fund opposed the application on grounds that N.Y. Insurance Law § 16 asserted by the superintendent as authority for such a liquidation was, as applied, inconsistent with and repugnant to § 3029(c)(5) of the Federal Labor-Management Relations Act, 29 U.S.C.S. § 186 (c)(5). The trial court granted the petition and the trustees appealed. The court affirmed, holding that clearly, the intent of Congress was not to pre-empt the field, but to leave in the state a large measure of regulatory power over these insurance funds. The state insurance department was doing nothing to prevent the "carrying out" of the welfare fund agreement but was exercising a power as to liquidation, a subject which no federal act dealt with.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court, which affirmed the trial court order granting a petition by the superintendent of insurance for an order directing the superintendent to take possession of the trust property and to liquidate and dissolve the trust was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Insurance -- employee welfare funds -- Congress did not pre-empt whole field of legislation in regard to employee welfare funds in Federal Labor-Management Relations Act -- article XVI of State Insurance Law not inconsistent with or repugnant to provisions of Federal Labor-Management Relations Act, pursuant to which trust fund was established in connection with collective bargaining agreement -- State Superintendent of Insurance had power to liquidate Fund.

1. Congress did not in the Federal Labor-Management Relations Act pre-empt the whole field of legislation in regard to employee welfare funds and did not show an intent to displace local and not inconsistent insurance regulation laws.

2. Article XVI of the State Insurance Law is not, as applied here, inconsistent with and repugnant to section 302 (subd. [c], par. [5]) of the Federal Labor-Management Relations Act (U. S. Code, tit. 29, § 186, subd. [c], par. [5]) pursuant to which a trust fund known as "United Construction Workers, United Mine Workers of America-S. H. Pomeroy Company Welfare Fund" was established in connection with a collective bargaining agreement made in 1957.

3. Accordingly, when the employer went out of business, the State Superintendent of Insurance had the power under article XVI of the Insurance Law to take possession of the property and liquidate the affairs of and dissolve the Fund.

People v. Williams


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 382; 179 N.E.2d 487; 223 N.Y.S.2d 474; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 855


November 13, 1961, Argued  
December 7, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and a new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People sought review of an order of the Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York, Appellate Part, in the Second Judicial Department, which reversed, on the law and the facts, a judgment of a magistrates' court convicting defendant of a violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 975 for possession of comptroller's ribbons used in the operation of the game called "policy."


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the complaint charging him was too broad in its scope to fairly apprise him of the charge, and that a violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 975 could only be proven by evidence of possession of material used in the actual wagering on the game of policy. He also contended that the statute conferring jurisdiction over gambling offenses on the magistrates' court was unconstitutional. The court found that although the heading of the complaint referred to possession of policy slips, the body of the complaint charged defendant with possession of a writing, paper, and document commonly used in carrying on, promoting and playing the game commonly called "policy." It further specified that defendant had in his possession 5 comptroller's ribbons. Clearly, defendant knew that he was being charged with possession of the comptroller's ribbons, and that such possession violated § 975. Defendant was properly informed an the charge enabled him to prepare for trial. The court also noted that the jurisdiction issue had been decided. The court decided that the appellate court's order reversing the magistrates' court's decision had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and ordered a new trial.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- policy -- information entitled "Possession of Policy Slips" sufficient although it did not charge possession of policy slips but did charge possession of comptroller's ribbons -- section 102-a of New York City Criminal Courts Act, vesting Magistrates' Courts in City of New York with jurisdiction, not unconstitutional.

1. Defendant was convicted of a violation of section 975 of the Penal Law, having been found guilty of possession of materials "used in carrying on, promoting or playing the game commonly called 'policy'". Although the heading of the information stated "Possession of Policy Slips", the body of the information charged defendant with possession "of a writing, paper, and document representing and being a record of any chance, share etc." It further stated that defendant had in his possession five comptroller's ribbons, used in the operation of the game called "policy". There was no charge that defendant possessed policy slips. The information was sufficient. Defendant knew that he was being charged with possession of the comptroller's ribbons, and that such possession violated section 975 of the Penal Law.

2. Section 102-a of the New York City Criminal Courts Act, which vests the Magistrates' Courts in the City of New York with jurisdiction over this crime, is not unconstitutional.

 

430 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Greenburgh v. Bobandal Realties, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 414; 179 N.E.2d 702; 223 N.Y.S.2d 857; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 860


October 17, 1961, Argued  
December 7, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and complaint dismissed, with costs in this court and in the Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which reversed a trial court's judgment dismissing respondent town's complaint against the corporation to enjoin the corporation from using two parcels of land for purposes allegedly not permitted uses under the town's zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: At the time the zoning ordinance at issue was in effect, the corporation was operating a restaurant and bar on a parcel of land and a swimming pool on an adjoining parcel of land. The parcels were situated in a one-family residence district, and that the uses described were prohibited uses in such a district. The town claimed that the corporation never acquired any rights by virtue of their prior use, since such use was at all times in violation of two prior zoning ordinances enacted in 1924 and 1932. The trial court dismissed the complaint for failure of the ordinances to be personally served on the corporation or their predecessors in title as the act expressly required. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court then reversed the appellate court's order and found that the ordinances cited by the town did not apply due to procedural defects in their enactment. The court further found that the evidence was clear that the corporation's activities constituted a prior nonconforming use which it was entitled to continue. There was no ground upon which the town would be entitled to the injunction which it sought, and the complaint was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's order and dismissed the town's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- prior nonconforming use -- defendants entitled to continue prior nonconforming uses after enactment of zoning ordinance -- prior use was not in violation of prior zoning ordinance since such prior ordinance did not take effect because it was not personally served upon defendants or predecessors in title (Town Law, § 142-a; L. 1922, ch. 322).

1. The complaint in an action by a town to enjoin defendants from using two parcels of land for purposes allegedly not permitted uses under the town's present zoning ordinance is dismissed. At the time the zoning ordinance took effect, defendant corporation was operating a restaurant and bar and a swimming pool on parcels situated in a one-family residence district. Such uses are prohibited uses in such a district. Since they were prior nonconforming uses, defendants are entitled to the continued use of the property contrary to the provisions of the ordinance.

2. The prior use was not in violation of a prior zoning ordinance of 1924. Section 142-a of the Town Law (L. 1919, ch. 218) provided that: "Ordinances which the town board may adopt shall be published before they shall go into effect in a newspaper published in the town, if any, and also in such other newspaper or newspapers as may be designated by the town board, and posted in at least three public places in the town. Such ordinances shall take effect ten days after the date of such publication, if any, and posting." Section 142-a was amended (L. 1922, ch. 322) by the addition of a new subdivision 18 which for the first time conferred upon town boards the power to enact zoning ordinances. That new subdivision provided that such a zoning ordinance "shall take effect from the date of its service as against a person served personally with a copy thereof, certified by the town clerk under the corporate seal of the town, and showing the date of its passage and entry in the minutes." The 1924 zoning ordinance, enacted pursuant to the authority provided by said chapter 322 of the Laws of 1922, did not take effect because it was not personally served upon defendants or their predecessors in title as that statute expressly required.

People v. Codarre


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 361; 179 N.E.2d 475; 223 N.Y.S.2d 457; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 890


October 17, 1961, Argued  
November 30, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and matter remitted to the County Court of Dutchess County for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed by permission from an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed an order of the trial court denying defendant's motion for a writ of error coram nobis to vacate a judgment of conviction rendered against him nearly 20 years earlier for murder in the second degree. By the coram nobis proceeding, defendant prayed that his guilty plea and sentence be vacated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 13 years old when he withdrew his plea of not guilty, pleaded guilty to murder in the second degree, and was sentenced to 30 years to life. In the coram nobis petition, defendant prayed for the guilty plea and sentence to be vacated and requested a hearing, claiming that because of his youth and epileptic condition, his plea was not voluntary and he was therefore denied due process of law. The court reversed the trial court's denial of the petition without a hearing, holding that defendant's allegations stated a case for coram nobis relief. Defendant's guilty plea had been accepted despite medical evidence before the trial court that the killing had occurred while defendant was in the throes of an epileptic rage or furor attack. The court held that the taking of a guilty plea from defendant, a child, called for an extreme measure of caution and at least certainty of guilty and of the complete absence of any plausible defense. Because defendant appeared to have such a defense and insufficient consideration was given to it, the court remanded the action to the trial court for a hearing on the coram nobis petition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, which affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a writ of error coram nobis to vacate his guilty plea and a judgment of conviction rendered against him nearly 20 years earlier for murder in the second degree. The court further remitted the matter to the trial court for a trial of the allegations of the petition.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- coram nobis -- guilty plea by epileptic -- defendant entitled to hearing in coram nobis proceeding where he alleges that he was denied due process of law when he was permitted to plead guilty to murder in second degree when he was 13 years old and medical expert had stated that killing took place while defendant was in throes of epileptic rage or furor attack.

Defendant, then 13 years old and charged with murder in the first degree, was allowed to plead guilty to murder in the second degree and given a sentence of 30 years to life. By this coram nobis proceeding he asked that the guilty plea and sentence be vacated and demanded a hearing, alleging that he had been deprived of due process of law when, at the time he pleaded guilty, an opinion by a medical expert that the killing had taken place while defendant was in the throes of an epileptic rage or furor attack was before the court. The taking of a guilty plea of murder from so young a defendant called for an extreme measure of caution and at least certainty of guilt and of the complete absence of any plausible defense. On a trial of the allegations of the petition, it might be found that this defendant had such a defense and that insufficient consideration was given to it. The matter should be remitted to the County Court for a trial of the allegations of the petition.

Court of Appeals of New York

433 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


New York State Thruway Authority v. Ashley Motor Court, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 151; 176 N.E.2d 566; 218 N.Y.S.2d 640; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 1083


June 7, 1961, Argued  
July 7, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant motel appealed from a judgment of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed a judgment of the lower court in favor of plaintiff thruway authority (authority), regarding the constitutionality of N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 361-a, which restricted the erection of billboards and other advertising devices along the thruway.


OVERVIEW: The motel argued that § 361-a was invalid because it was not reasonably related to the public health, morals, or safety, and because it constituted a taking of property rights without compensation. The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate division. The court determined that there could be no doubt that the statute was reasonably related to a legitimate legislative purpose because it was aimed at rendering the thruway safe for the traveling public by providing maximum visibility and by preventing unreasonable distractions. The court concluded that police power was the least limitable of the powers of government and extended to all of the great public needs, and if the end desired was within the power of the state and the means used were reasonably suited to that end, it was no objection that the rights of private property were thereby curtailed. The court explained that because § 361-a represented a constitutional exercise of the state's police power, the injunction was properly issued to require the motel to remove the advertising device that it was maintaining.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate division, in favor of the authority, regarding the constitutionality of the statute.


HEADNOTES

Highways -- billboards -- section 361-a of Public Authorities Law prohibiting erection of billboards or other advertising devices near New York State Thruway without written permit is not unconstitutional -- statute aimed at rendering Thruway safe for traveling public -- defendants not deprived of property without due process of law -- statute represents exercise of State's police power.

1. Section 361-a of the Public Authorities Law prohibits the erection of any billboard or other advertising device within a stated distance of the nearest edge of the New York State Thruway pavement unless a written permit is granted by the Thruway Authority and gives the Authority (subd. 3) the power to adopt regulations for the issuance of permits for advertising devices (a) "To provide for maximum visibility"; (b) "To prevent unreasonable distraction" of motor vehicle operators; (c) "To prevent confusion with regard to traffic lights, signs or signals" or other interference with the effectiveness of traffic regulations; (d) "To preserve and enhance the natural scenic beauty or the aesthetic features of the thruway system", and (e) "To promote maximum safety, comfort and well-being of the users of the thruway." Pursuant to that statute defendants were properly enjoined from continuing the use of a sign erected by them along the Thruway without having a permit. The statute is not unconstitutional. It was aimed at rendering the Thruway safe for the traveling public by providing for maximum visibility and by preventing unreasonable distractions and is reasonably related to a legitimate legislative purpose.

2. It is not necessary to determine whether the preservation of "the natural scenic beauty" would of itself be a sufficient basis for the legislation. This is only one of the objectives and standards which the Authority is directed to have in mind in adopting regulations for the issuance of permits.

3. Defendants are not being deprived of their property without due process of law. Although the sign existed at another location at a prior time, it was relocated and placed in its present position sometime after the effective date of the statute. This constituted the erection of a new sign. Moreover, it was the construction of the Thruway which created the element of value in the land abutting the road.

4. Even if, however, defendants possessed valid and subsisting property rights which the legislation abrogated, this would not provide a sufficient basis for declaring the statute unconstitutional. The statute represents a constitutional exercise of the State's police power.

 

434 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Engel v. Vitale


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 174; 176 N.E.2d 579; 218 N.Y.S.2d 659; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 1086


May 25, 1961, Argued  
July 7, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, taxpayers and parents of public school children, sought review of an order of the Supreme Court in Nassau County (New York) that dismissed their complaint against respondent school district board members (board) that alleged that the adoption of a practice that combined act of allegiance to the American flag by school children with an act of reverence to God violated U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: The board instructed its teaching staff that, at the commencement of each school day, the act of allegiance to the American flag was to be joined with the following act of reverence to God: "Almighty God, we acknowledge our dependence upon Thee, and we beg Thy blessings upon us, our parents, our teachers and our country." Taxpayers and parents of school children brought suit for an order directing the board to discontinue the practice on the ground that it constituted an establishment of religion in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I. The trial court denied the petition and remanded the matter to the board of education. The decision was affirmed on appeal and the case was remanded to the trial court with an order that it be dismissed. The trial court dismissed the case and the taxpayers and parents sought review. In affirming the decision, the court held that U.S. Const. amend. I did not forbid as an "establishment of religion" a simple declaration of belief in God. As such, the court found that the prayer at issue was not an unconstitutional establishment of religion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the complaint and held that the prayer at issue made a simple declaration of belief in God that did not constitute an unconstitutional establishment of religion under the First Amendment of the United States Constitution.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- prayer in public school -- provision for recitation of prayer in public school, recommended by Board of Regents, not in violation of First Amendment of United States Constitution or of article I (§ 3) of New York State Constitution.

Pursuant to a recommendation of the Board of Regents, the board members of a public school district instructed the teaching staff to adopt the practice of joining with the pledge of allegiance to the flag the following prayer. "Almighty God, we acknowledge our dependence upon Thee, and we beg Thy blessings upon us, our parents, our teachers and our Country". Provisions have been made to insure that no pupil need take part in or be present during the saying of the prayer. Providing for the saying of this prayer in the schools is not in violation of the First Amendment of the United States Constitution or of section 3 of article I of the New York State Constitution. 

 

435 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


La Belle Creole Intl., S. A. v. AG of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 192; 176 N.E.2d 705; 219 N.Y.S.2d 1; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 1087


May 17, 1961, Argued  
July 7, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorney general appealed from the order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which vacated his subpoena duces tecum upon petitioner foreign corporation's president to testify and produce foreign corporation's books and records.


OVERVIEW: A foreign corporation was in the business of providing a service for the placing of orders for liquor by United States residents traveling abroad and of arranging for the delivery of the liquor to their homes duty free. The attorney general served a subpoena duces tecum on the foreign corporation's president to testify and produce the foreign corporation's books and records. The foreign corporation brought a proceeding to vacate the subpoena duces tecum. It argued that (1) the subpoena was unconstitutionally vague and indefinite and (2) it was not subject to service of process because it was a foreign corporation not doing business in the state. The appellate division vacated the subpoena duces tecum. The attorney general appealed. He argued that he was authorized to investigate the possibility of foreign corporation's violation of N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law §§ 102(1) and 130. The attorney general could serve a subpoena duces tecum on the foreign corporation's president as the attorney general was authorized to investigate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate division because the foreign corporation was not immune from investigation by attorney general in an inquiry to determine whether it was violating the laws of the state.


HEADNOTES

Corporations -- foreign corporations -- subpoenas -- subpoena served by Attorney-General (Executive Law, § 63, subd. 12) on president of petitioner, Panamanian corporation with principal place of business in Haiti and engaged in business of delivering liquor duty free, not defective for failing to show matters under investigation or in what manner requested documents are relevant and material -- foreign corporation subject to service of this process -- foreign corporation's immunity from civil suit does not give it immunity from Attorney-General's investigation.

1. The petitioner, a Panamanian corporation with its principal place of business in Haiti, is in the business of providing a service for the placing of orders for liquor by residents of this country traveling abroad and of arranging for the delivery of the liquor to their homes duty free. The Attorney-General served a subpoena, pursuant to subdivision 12 of section 63 of the Executive Law, upon petitioner's president in New York City requiring petitioner to give testimony in an inquiry by the Attorney-General to determine whether an application should be made or an action instituted to enjoin petitioner "from the commission of persistently fraudulent or illegal acts" and directing the production of corporate books and records. The subpoena is not defective for failing to show what matters are in fact under investigation or in what manner the requested documents are relevant and material to such investigation. Upon this preliminary motion, the Attorney-General need only show that the records and books demanded bear a reasonable relation to the subject matter under investigation and to the public purpose to be achieved.

2. The corporation is subject to the service of this process although it is a foreign corporation. Where the purpose of the proceeding is to protect citizens of the State from potentially dangerous consequences, less evidence of the corporation's doing business in the State is required than might otherwise be required.

3. The issuance of a subpoena is not rendered improper because it may produce the evidence required to establish that petitioner is doing business in New York.

4. Even if petitioner's contacts with this State were less than necessary to justify the maintenance of a civil suit, petitioner would still be amenable to the subpoena served upon its president by the Attorney-General in connection with the investigation. A foreign corporation's immunity from civil suit in New York on the ground that it is not here doing business does not give it immunity from investigation by the Attorney-General in an inquiry to determine whether it is violating the laws of this State.

 

436 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Schulman v. People


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 249; 176 N.E.2d 817; 219 N.Y.S.2d 241; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 1094


June 1, 1961, Argued  
July 7, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, with costs, and the order of the County Court reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a decision from the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which granted the motion of respondent, the State of New York, to dismiss their complaint alleging that the state had no authority to regulate advertising along a public highway by appropriating property under N.Y. High. Law § 30 (1944).


OVERVIEW: N.Y. High. Law § 30 authorized the state to condemn property in conjunction with highways for other purposes to improve safety conditions on the state highway system. From this, the state determined that it was able to condemn a negative easement under § 30, to eliminate on payment of compensation what other statutes prohibited under the police power. The state read the purpose of § 30 as being the elimination of advertising along public highways. The state was previously unsuccessful in passing other laws to achieve the same purpose. The property owners brought an action against the state, which the appellate court dismissed on the state's motion. The court reversed. The court held that § 30 was not designed or intended to authorize the condemnation of easements for the purpose of eliminating advertising under the "other purposes" clause because § 30 referred to specific adjuncts such as drains, ditches, gravel pits, and stone quarries. In addition, other statutes regulated or prohibited advertising signs on other roads and there were four abortive attempts to obtain similar legislation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's grant of the state's motion to dismiss in the property owners' complaint alleging that the state did not have authority to appropriate property to regulate advertising.


HEADNOTES

Highways -- prohibition of billboards -- section 30 of Highway Law, which provided that Superintendent of Public Works might acquire by appropriation property, including easements, necessary for construction of State highways for stated purposes and "to improve safety conditions on the state highway system", was not intended to permit State to condemn property in form of negative easements along State highway for purpose of prohibiting advertising signs.

Section 30 of the Highway Law provided that the Superintendent of Public Works might acquire by appropriation any and all property, including easements necessary for the construction, reconstruction and improvement of State highways "including the appropriation of property for drains, ditches, spoil banks, gravel pits and stone quarries; also for the removal of obstructions, improvement of sight distances; * * * and for other purposes to improve safety conditions on the state highway system." That statute was not intended to permit the State to condemn, on payment of just compensation, property rights in the form of negative easements along a portion of Route 17 in Sullivan County for the purpose of prohibiting advertising signs capable of being seen from the State highway.

 

437 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


I. L. F. Y. Co. v. Temporary State Housing Rent Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 263; 176 N.E.2d 822; 219 N.Y.S.2d 249; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 1096


June 7, 1961, Argued  
July 7, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which dismissed an action against appellees, state housing rent commission and others, that challenged the validity and constitutionality of the N.Y. Emergency Housing Rent Control Law § 4(4)(a)(1)(v).


OVERVIEW: The landlord bought an apartment house. Two months later, the legislature enacted the N.Y. Emergency Housing Rent Control Law § 4(4)(a)(1)(v), which provided that no application for a maximum rent increase could be made until six months after the date of purchase of a rental property, and that any increase could not be implemented prior to one year from the date of purchase. In affirming the judgment, the court first cemented the validity of the statute. The court explained that it was presumed that the legislature acted based on facts found to warrant the action. Besides this presumption the court noted a slew of facts, generated by two commissions, relating to the crisis in the rental housing situation, which girded the legislative fiat. Furthermore, the court explained that a well-founded fear of future trouble could justify present legislation. The court similarly was not disposed to favor the landlord's claim that the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which dismissed the landlord's challenge to an emergency rent control act.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- fixing rent on sale price -- provisions of Emergency Housing Rent Control Law (L. 1961, ch. 337), prohibiting application for adjustment of rent on sale price until six months from date of sale and providing that adjustment may not be effective before one year from date of sale or prior to date of issue of order, and that such provisions applied to applications pending when law became effective, not unconstitutional -- provisions reasonably necessary for public welfare.

1. By chapter 337 of the Laws of 1961, which became a law on April 6, 1961, there was added to the Emergency Housing Rent Control Law a provision that "No application for adjustment of maximum rent valuation based upon a sale price valuation shall be filed by the landlord under this subparagraph prior to six months from the date of such sale of the property. In addition, no adjustment ordered by the commission based upon such sales price valuation shall be effective prior to one year from the date of such sale." As revised in 1961, the law forbade retroactive changes in rent, and the 1961 amendments were applicable to pending proceedings. The statutory changes are not unconstitutional. They were enacted following investigation by the Legislature. The Legislature was aware that apartments could be and were being sold continuously at inflated prices to take advantage of the higher rents. The writing of these precautions into law was reasonably necessary for the public welfare. Even if there were no record of any investigation, the courts would assume factual support for the legislation to exist.

2. Plaintiff's constitutional rights were not infringed when the 1961 statute was made to apply to premises purchased at an earlier date. It had no interest in any particular rule so vested as to entitle it to keep the rule unchanged. The applicability and validity of statutes are determined as of the date the court makes its decision.

 

438 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Connecticut General Life Ins. Co. v. Superintendent of Ins.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 42; 176 N.E.2d 63; 217 N.Y.S.2d 39; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 1164


April 20, 1961, Argued  
June 1, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, with costs in all courts, and matter remitted to Special Term for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), denying a motion by appellant for summary judgment and granting a cross motion of respondent for summary judgment in an action concerning appellant's right to acquire a controlling stock interest in a fire or casualty insurance company.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that N.Y. Ins. Law §§ 42(3) and 193(2) should not be construed to prohibit it from acquiring a controlling interest in a fire or casualty insurance company. Respondent asserted that it determined that the statutory proscription was absolute and unqualified prohibiting a licensed life insurer from doing, either directly or through a stock-controlled subsidiary, any fire or casualty business. The court held that the Legislature did not intend that the limitations of N.Y. Ins. Law §§ 42(3) and 193(2) be extended by implication to cover parent-subsidiary situations. There was no recognizable basis for forbidding appellant's investment. N.Y. Ins. Law § 90(1) should have been construed to allow the investment.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant's motion for summary judgment and granting respondent's cross motion for summary judgment was reversed on grounds of erroneous statutory construction by respondent.


HEADNOTES

Insurance -- foreign life insurer -- acquisition of fire or casualty company -- Insurance Law ( § 42, subd. 3; § 193, subd. 2), which forbids foreign life insurance company licensed in this State from engaging in business of writing fire or casualty insurance, does not prohibit foreign life insurance company from acquiring controlling stock interest in company doing fire or casualty insurance business.

1. Section 42 (subd. 3) and section 193 (subd. 2) of the Insurance Law, which forbid a foreign life insurance company licensed in this State from engaging in the business of writing fire or casualty insurance, were not intended to prohibit such foreign life insurance company from acquiring a controlling stock interest in a company doing a fire or casualty insurance business. By purchasing a controlling interest in a fire or casualty company, the parent life insurance company is not actually engaging in that business.

2. Section 90 of the Insurance Law, which regulates the investments of out-of-State insurers, does not interfere with the acquisition of a controlling stock interest in another insurer so long as the parent company has sufficient investments which comply strictly with the investment limitations imposed on domestic companies and a sufficient surplus for policyholders.

Fisher v. State


Claim No. 36252


Court of Appeals of New York


10 N.Y.2d 60; 176 N.E.2d 72; 217 N.Y.S.2d 52; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 1165


May 22, 1961, Argued  
June 1, 1961, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an unlawfully convicted party, appealed from a judgment upon an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Third Judicial Department (New York), which unanimously affirmed an order dismissing appellant's amended claim against the state for damage he suffered when an Assistant District Attorney tortiously presented false information to juries, resulting in an unlawful conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was unlawfully convicted after an Assistant District Attorney of New York County tortiously presented false information to both a Grand Jury and to a trial jury. The conviction was later set aside in coram nobis proceedings. Appellant's action against the state brought on the theory of respondeat superior, contending that the Assistant District Attorney was acting as an agent of the state, was dismissed for failure to state a cause of action, and that judgment was unanimously affirmed. Appellant was granted leave to appeal, and the court affirmed the judgment. The court found that pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 2, which defined both "state officer" and "local officer", the Assistant District Attorney was not an officer of the state. Additionally, the court found that the representation of the Assistant District Attorney was limited to a specific county and was not a state-wide role. Thus, the court concluded that the Assistant District Attorney's actions were not attributable to the state.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirming an order that dismissed appellant's amended claim against the state for tortious acts of the Assistant District Attorney was affirmed, with costs.


HEADNOTES

State -- claim against State -- State officers -- Assistant District Attorney of New York County not "state officer" (Public Officers Law, § 2) -- State may not be held liable on theory of respondeat superior for alleged presentation of false information to Grand Jury.

A claim against the State in which claimant alleged that he suffered damage when an Assistant District Attorney of New York County tortiously presented false information to a Grand Jury and to a trial jury, resulting in an unlawful conviction, which was later set aside in coram nobis proceedings, was properly dismissed. The Assistant District Attorney was not a "state officer" (Public Officers Law, § 2) and the State may not, therefore, be held liable on the theory of respondeat superior.

 

440 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Richmond County News, Inc.


Court of Appeals of New York


9 N.Y.2d 578; 175 N.E.2d 681; 216 N.Y.S.2d 369; 1961 N.Y. LEXIS 1615


Argued March 23, 1961  
May 25, 1961. - Decided



DISPOSITION:  Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant magazine wholesaler was convicted of selling and distributing an allegedly obscene magazine in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141. The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York) reversed finding that the proof failed to establish that defendant had knowledge of the magazine's obscene character. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The magazine at issue contained numerous pictures and cartoons of nude or semi-nude women and numerous descriptions and depictions of sexual arousal and satisfaction. The court affirmed the reversal of the conviction, holding that the magazine was not obscene. The court held that the prohibitions of § 1141 applied only to "hard-core pornography." Under § 1141, the test of the obscene, of the pornographic, was not in the tendency or appeal of the material, but rather in its content objectively appraised. The court held that the obscene focused predominantly upon what was sexually morbid, grossly perverse, and bizarre, without any artistic or scientific purpose or justification. Recognizable by the insult it invariably offered to sex and to the human spirit, it was to be differentiated from the bawdy and the ribald. Depicting dirt for dirt's sake, the obscene was the vile, rather than the coarse, the blow to sense, not merely to sensibility. The court held that the magazine here contained nothing which smacked of sick and blatantly perverse sexuality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the appellate division overturning defendant's conviction for selling and distributing an allegedly obscene magazine.


HEADNOTES

Crimes - obscenity - information charging defendant with selling and distributing obscene magazine properly dismissed - magazine not "obscene" (Penal Law, § 1141).

An order of the Appellate Division which reversed a judgment of the Court of Special Sessions of the City of New York convicting defendant of a violation of section 1141 of the Penal Law on an information which charged it with selling and distributing an allegedly obscene magazine, and dismissed the information, is affirmed. The magazine was not "obscene".
