Gordon v. McGovern


Court of Appeals of New York


308 N.Y. 989; 127 N.E.2d 844; 1955 N.Y. LEXIS 1215


Argued April 25, 1955  
June 2, 1955, decided


HEADNOTES

Abandoned property - unclaimed surplus moneys from sale of pledged articles - pawnbrokers - municipal corporations - section 1301 of Abandoned Property Law requires pawnbrokers realizing surplus moneys from sale of pawned articles to pay over such moneys to State - Charter of City of Buffalo empowered common council to enact ordinances to [***4] license and regulate business of pawnbrokers - ordinance of City of Buffalo regulated sale of unredeemed pledges - in action by pawnbroker for judgment declaring section 1301 of Abandoned Property Law not applicable to City of Buffalo, Appellate Division stated that statute was valid and did apply to City of Buffalo and was not in conflict with charter or ordinances of city - judgment affirmed.

 

553 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


RKO-Keith-Orpheum Theatres, Inc. v. New York


Court of Appeals of New York


308 N.Y. 493; 127 N.E.2d 284; 1955 N.Y. LEXIS 979


Argued March 3, 1955.  
May 26, 1955, decided



DISPOSITION: CONWAY, Ch. J., DESMOND, DYE, FULD and FROESSEL, JJ., concur; BURKE, J., taking no part.

Ordered accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which modified an order granting the city's motion for summary judgment. Plaintiff theaters contested direction to collect an entire additional cent tax in instances where only half or a major fraction of a cent was due.


OVERVIEW: The theaters sought a declaratory judgment determining that the direction in the New York City Amusement Tax, enacted by Local Law No. 37 of 1954 of the City of New York, requiring the collection of an entire additional cent tax in instances where only half or a major fraction of a cent was due, was void. The trial court granted the city summary judgment and the appellate court reversed. The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and reinstated the judgment of the trial court. The court noted that the enabling act limited the amount of tax which could be charged by the city to five percent and that the result of the breakage was to require payment of more than five percent in some instances. The burden of paying the admissions tax fell upon theater patrons and the custom of paying an extra cent was found to have a de minimis impact on the patrons. The court concluded that the five percent tax was subject to the manner of handling breakage usual in commercial transactions. Section B32-5.0 of the Administrative Code, which prohibited charging an amount greater than the ticket price for tickets, did not preclude the future imposition of taxes pursuant to an enabling act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate court and reinstated the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to the city.


HEADNOTES

Taxation - municipal corporations [***2] - New York City Amusement Tax - (1) New York City local law, providing that, in respect to 5% tax on admission charges to amusements, where tax includes fraction of one cent, full cent shall be paid when fraction is one-half cent or more, is valid, notwithstanding that, mathematically, payment of more than 5% admissions tax required at some times - (2) considered from viewpoint of person paying doctrine of de minimis non curat lex applies - (3) Legislature intended to adopt manner of handling "breakage" usual in commercial transactions - (4) New York City Administrative Code (§ B32-5.0) does not preclude municipal admissions tax.

1. New York City Local Law No. 37 of 1954 imposes a tax of 5% upon admission charges to certain places of amusement and provides that "Where the tax to be paid by a patron includes a fraction of one cent, the fraction shall not be paid when it is less than one-half cent and a full cent shall be paid when the fraction is one-half cent or more" (Administrative Code, § G46-2.0 subd. d). The provision which directs the collection of an entire additiona cent tax in instances where only half or a major fraction of a cent is due, is valid, notwithstanding [***3] that the enabling statutes (L. 1947, ch. 278, as amd.) limit the amount of the tax which may be charged by the municipality to 5% and that the result of this tax, in certain instances, is to require payment of more than a 5% admissions tax.

2. In deciding whether the doctrine of de minimis non curat lex should be applied, the problem should be studied from the viewpoint of the purchaser of a theatre ticket. Thus considered, the disposition of the fractional parts of a cent is inconsequential and de minimis.

3. When the Legislature authorized municipalities to levy these taxes at 5%, it meant 5% subject to the manner of handling "breakage" which is usual in commercial transactions.

4. Section B32-5.0 of the Administrative Code prohibiting the charging of more for a theatre ticket than the regular or established price, plus the amount of any tax imposed by the United States Government, was not intended to prohibit the levying or collection of taxes which might validly be levied upon admissions pursuant to law.

 

554 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ercole


Court of Appeals of New York


308 N.Y. 425; 126 N.E.2d 543; 1955 N.Y. LEXIS 989


Argued February 25, 1955.  
April 21, 1955, decided



DISPOSITION: CONWAY, Ch. J., and DYE, J., concur with BURKE, J.; FULD, J., concurs in a separate opinion; DESMOND, J., dissents in an opinion in which FROESSEL and VAN VOORHIS, JJ., concur.

Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the dismissal of defendant's conviction for grand larceny by the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York).


OVERVIEW: In defendant's trial for grand larceny, the trial court allowed the state to amend the indictment to allege false or fraudulent representation or pretense in the course of accomplishing, or in aid of, or in facilitating the theft. N.Y. Penal Law § 1290-a(1) stated that evidence of the defendant's false or fraudulent representation or pretense could not be received at the trial unless the indictment or information alleged such representation or pretense. The original indictment did not so allege, and an amendment was allowed during the state's case. The appellate court reversed the conviction, and the court affirmed. The court held that the indictment, prepared according to N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 276, could not have been amended except for a variance as to (1) time, (2) name or (3) description of any place, person or thing, and then only subject to the condition that the defense would not be prejudiced on the merits under N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 293. The liberal amendment allowed by N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 295-j was applicable only to the amendment of a simplified indictment, which was not used in defendant's prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's reversal of defendant's grand larceny conviction.


HEADNOTES

Crimes - indictments - amendments - (1) Code of Criminal Procedure (§ 295-j) authorizes amendment of "simplified indictment" only - (2) "long-form indictment" (Code Crim. Pro., § 276), charging larceny, could not be amended under section 295-j to conform to proof by adding counts charging larceny by use of fraudulent representations - (3) "long-form indictment" may be amended under Code of Criminal Procedure (§ 293).

1. Section 295-j of the Code of Criminal Procedure, providing that, upon the trial of an indictment, the court [***2] may direct the indictment to be amended according to the proof, was enacted as part of an over-all legislative scheme to authorize prosecution by "simplified indictments" (Code Crim. Pro., part IV, tit. V, ch. III-A), and authorizes an amendment of a "simplified indictment" only.

2. Accordingly where, during the examination of the People's first witness, defendant objected to further interrogation on the ground that the indictment failed to allege, as required by section 1290-a of the Penal Law, that defendant made use of a fraudulent representation in the course of accomplishing the charged theft, the "long-form indictment" (Code Crim. Pro., part IV, tit. V, ch. II, § 276) charging counts of larceny could not be amended, pursuant to section 295-j of the code, to conform to the proof by adding counts charging larceny by use of fraudulent representation.

3. A "long-form indictment" may be amended pursuant to section 293 of the Code of Criminal Procedure (part IV, tit. V, ch. III), but only to correct a variance as to time, name or description of any place, person or thing and then only subject to the condition that the defense will not be prejudiced on the merits.

Somers v. Covey


Court of Appeals of New York


308 N.Y. 798; 125 N.E.2d 862; 1955 N.Y. LEXIS 1064


Argued January 12, 1955

HEADNOTES

Taxation - tax liens, tax sales and tax titles - incompetents - about one year after deed was [***4] delivered to town in in rem proceeding to foreclose tax lien, committee of incompetent-owner moved to open default and vacate judgment of foreclosure - Tax Law ( § 165-h, subd. 7) provided that deed should be presumptive evidence that action and proceedings were regular and, after two years from date of recording of deed, presumption should become conclusive, and that no action to set aside such deed might be maintained unless action commenced and lis pendens filed prior to time that presumption became conclusive - County Court denied committee's motion - in Court of Appeals committee argued that statutory limitation of time to redeem was tolled because of known mental condition of incompetent, and that Tax Law (art. VII-A) providing for foreclosure of tax liens in rem was unconstitutional as to incompetent - town argued that proper procedure to set aside deed was by action, and that committee had failed to bring action within two-year period - order properly affirmed.

557 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


United Press Assos. v. Valente


Court of Appeals of New York


308 N.Y. 71; 123 N.E.2d 777; 1954 N.Y. LEXIS 920


Argued November 16, 1953.  
December 31, 1954, decided



DISPOSITION: LEWIS, Ch. J., and CONWAY, J., concur with FULD, J.; DESMOND, J., concurs in result in a separate opinion; FROESSEL, J., dissents in an opinion in which DYE, J., concurs; VAN VOORHIS, J., taking no part.

Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner media organizations brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding in the Supreme Court, New York County (New York) against respondent judge, who had entered an order excluding the public from attending a criminal trial. The lower appellate courts upheld the judge's order and denied petitioners' art. 78 application. Petitioners appealed, arguing that they had been entitled to compel the judge to open the trial to the public.


OVERVIEW: In the course of a criminal case, the judge excluded the public, including petitioners, from attendance at the trial. Petitioners brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding to enjoin the judge from enforcing his exclusionary order. On review, the intermediate appellate courts affirmed the judge's order. In defendant's appeal from his conviction, the court held that the judge's exclusionary order had deprived defendant of his right to a public trial. The issue in petitioners' appeal from the denial of their art. 78 petition was whether members of the public at large possessed an enforceable right to insist that defendant's trial be open to the public. The court held that petitioners were seeking to convert what was essentially the right of a particular accused into a privilege for every citizen, a privilege that the latter might have invoked independently of the rights of defendant. A consequence of petitioners' position would have been to permit defendant's rights to be determined in proceedings in which he was not a party and had no voice, as exemplified by the instant action. The decision upholding the denial of petitioners' application was thus affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court ruled against petitioners and affirmed the decision denying petitioners' art. 78 application. Petitioners possessed no independent right to insist that defendant's criminal trial be open to the public.


HEADNOTES

Trial - public trial - (1) trial judge, in interests of "good morals", excluded public and press from courtroom during People's case on trial for compulsory prostitution; application by press associations and newspaper publishers to restrain trial judge from carrying [***2] out such exclusion properly denied - (2) notwithstanding this appeal now moot, appeal entertained in view of importance of problem and principle involved - (3) constitutional guarantees of free speech and freedom of press not here involved - (4) press associations and newspaper publishers have no greater rights than every other citizen (Judiciary Law, § 4) to attend court sessions.

1. On the trial of a defendant on the charges of compulsory prostitution (Penal Law, § 2460) and other offenses of like character (Penal Law, § 1148), the trial judge, on his own motion, in the interests of "good morals", excluded the general public and the press from the courtroom during the presentation of the People's case. An application (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) by press associations and newspaper publishers to restrain the trial judge from carrying out such order of exclusion was properly denied.

2. Notwithstanding that the question on this appeal has become moot, the appeal should be entertained since the problem presented and the principle involved are of importance in the administration of the criminal law.

3. Constitutional guarantees of free speech and freedom of the press (U.S.  [***3] Const., 1st Amendt.; N.Y. Const., art. I, § 8) are not involved in this case.

4. Press associations and newspaper publishers have no greater rights than "every [other] citizen" to attend court sessions (Judiciary Law, § 4).

 

558 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mason


Court of Appeals of New York


307 N.Y. 570; 122 N.E.2d 916; 1954 N.Y. LEXIS 952


Argued October 5, 1954.  
November 18, 1954, decided



DISPOSITION: LEWIS, Ch. J., CONWAY, DESMOND, FULD, FROESSEL and VAN VOORHIS, JJ., concur.

Orders reversed, etc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three separate prosecutions the People sought review by permission from orders of the County Court of St. Lawrence County (New York), which, in each instance, reversed a judgment that convicted each defendant of operating an automobile while intoxicated, a misdemeanor and violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 70(5).


OVERVIEW: While the informations were not dismissed in so many words, it was clear that no further proceedings were contemplated. The cases presented the same or similar questions of law, namely, whether the county court erred as a matter of law in discrediting the magistrate's return as to proceedings had on arraignment. On review the court found that the county court erred as a matter of law when it chose to credit the affidavits of error. In dealing with the appeals the county court was not faced with a problem of credibility, but with a consideration of such legal error as appeared in the magistrate's returns. It was without power to discredit them as filed. When defendants submitted their appeals without having previously pointed out wherein the return was defective, they were deemed to have admitted their sufficiency and correctness. No such application was made and the magistrate's return as filed in each case was conclusive as to all controverted matters within the magistrate's knowledge. A plea of guilty admitted the allegations of the information and rendered further proof of such allegations unnecessary and immaterial.


OUTCOME: The orders of the county court were reversed and the judgment of conviction was affirmed as to each defendant.


HEADNOTES

Crimes - operating automobile while intoxicated - (1) County Court erred as matter of law in crediting allegations of affidavits on appeal where Magistrates filed returns controverting such allegations - (2) Magistrates' returns conclusive as to all controverted matters [***3] within their knowledge - (3) instructions complied with provisions of section 335-a of Code of Criminal Procedure - (4) alleged illegality of blood tests taken without consent not reviewable where pleas of guilty entered - (5) plea of guilty to information charging misdemeanor made it unnecessary to inform defendant of alternate methods of trial.

1. Upon an appeal to the County Court from judgments convicting each defendant of operating an automobile while intoxicated (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 70, subd. 5), the respective Magistrates filed returns definitely meeting and controverting the allegations of error assigned in the affidavits on appeal. The County Court erred as a matter of law in crediting the allegations of the affidavits and accepting them as a basis for reversal of the judgments.

2. The County Court was without power to discredit the returns as filed. When the appealing parties submitted their appeals without having previously pointed out wherein the returns, as filed, were defective, they must be deemed to have admitted their sufficiency and correctness. The Magistrates' returns were conclusive as to all controverted matters within their knowledge.

3.  [***4] The provisions of section 335-a of the Code of Criminal Procedure were sufficiently complied with as to each defendant, when two of them were instructed that upon conviction their drivers' licenses "would be suspended or revoked according to law", and when the statute was not only read to the third defendant but also explained.

4. The alleged illegality of blood tests taken without consent (Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 71-a) presented no question for review where pleas of guilty were entered.

5. A plea of guilty to an information charging a misdemeanor rendered it unnecessary for the Magistrate to inform defendant as to alternate methods of trial.

Dog Owners Asso. v. Hilleboe

Davis v. Board of Regents
